## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which most commonly arise in constitutive laws for elastic/plastic deformation with thermal softening or temperature-dependent stiffness. Likely relationships include sigma proportional to epsilon at small strain, plus nonlinear hardening in epsilon and decreasing strength/modulus with increasing T.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness changes with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (thermoelastic softening/stiffening with T)
- Nonlinear elastic (Murnaghan/Landau-type polynomial): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (finite-strain nonlinearity)
- Piecewise elastic–plastic idealization (yield then constant flow): sigma = Min(c0 * epsilon, c1 * exp(c2 * T)) (elastic up to a T-dependent yield stress)
- Ludwik-type strain hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (work hardening in epsilon with temperature factor)
- Hollomon-type power-law hardening with additive thermal term: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * exp(c3 * T) (hardening plus a T-dependent offset)
- Voce hardening with temperature-dependent saturation: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon))) * exp(c3 * T) (saturating hardening; temperature softening/stiffening)
- Ramberg–Osgood inverted form (stress as function of strain): sigma = c0 * (sqrt(1 + c1 * epsilon) - 1) (empirical elastic–plastic transition shape without explicit yield)
- Thermally activated flow-like log form (phenomenological): sigma = (c0 + c1 * log(c2 * epsilon + 1)) * exp(c3 * T) (log-hardening in epsilon with temperature factor)
- Johnson–Cook-like (without strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (plastic hardening with polynomial thermal softening)
- Zerilli–Armstrong-like (reduced, no strain-rate): sigma = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * T) + c3 * epsilon**c4 (exponential T softening term plus strain hardening)
- Rational hardening with thermal factor: sigma = c0 * (epsilon / (epsilon + c1)) * exp(c2 * T) (smooth saturation in epsilon; temperature scaling)
- Coupled thermo-mechanical cross term: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * T + c2 * epsilon**2 (explicit epsilon–T coupling when thermal effects depend on strain level)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic stiffness degradation with temperature → multiply an elastic term by exp(c*T) with c < 0 or use (c0 + c1*T) prefactor on epsilon
- Thermal softening of yield/flow stress → factors like (1 - c*T**n) or exp(c*T) with c < 0 multiplying a plastic hardening law
- Work hardening with diminishing incremental hardening → saturating forms in epsilon such as (1 - exp(c*epsilon)) or epsilon/(epsilon + c)
- Power-law hardening at moderate plastic strain → sigma contributions proportional to epsilon**n (n between 0 and 1 is common for many metals)
- Smooth elastic–plastic transition (no sharp yield) → concave functions like log(c*epsilon + 1) or sqrt(1 + c*epsilon) - 1
- Explicit thermo-mechanical coupling beyond simple scaling → include cross terms like epsilon*T or epsilon**n * T**m to capture strain-dependent thermal sensitivity
- Ensuring sigma(0,T) ≈ 0 for purely mechanical loading → structure sigma = epsilon * g(T,epsilon) rather than adding large T-only offsets
- High-temperature strength approaching a floor → add a small positive offset term c0 plus a decaying-in-T contribution c1*exp(c2*T) with c2 < 0
- Nonlinear elasticity at larger strain → include higher-order polynomial terms in epsilon (epsilon**2, epsilon**3) with coefficients that may depend on T

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci5)
============================================================
GT: c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + c4*epsilon**c5*exp(-c6/(c7*T)) + epsilon**c8*c9*(T - c10)
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) can be rewritten to expose its essential structure:

\[
\text{GT}=
\underbrace{61.3468690640\,\epsilon\left(-0.0507652233\,(T-278.1478751)+1\right)}_{\text{affine in }T \text{ times }\epsilon}
+\underbrace{98.5793949569\,\epsilon^{0.3178497444}\exp\!\left(-\frac{49.4558232675}{8.314\,T}\right)}_{\epsilon^{a}\exp(-k/T)}
+\underbrace{2.30405384882\,\epsilon^{1.45029456614}(T-278.1478751)}_{\epsilon^{b}\cdot(T-\text{const})}
\]

So GT is a sum of **three** terms with these key “signatures”:

1) A term **linear in \(\epsilon\)** and **affine in \(T\)**: \(\epsilon(\alpha T+\beta)\).  
2) A term \(\epsilon^{a}\exp(-k/T)\) with **negative** \(k/T\) in the exponent.  
3) A term \(\epsilon^{b}(T-\text{const})\): i.e., \(\epsilon^{b}T - (\text{const})\epsilon^{b}\). This necessarily includes a **\(\epsilon^{b}T\)** component.

Any candidate that cannot produce both (i) an \(\epsilon T\) term and (ii) an \(\epsilon^{b}T\) term (with \(b\neq 1\)), and (iii) an \(\exp(-k/T)\) term multiplied by \(\epsilon^{a}\), cannot match (even with domain restrictions), because these are analytic-in-\(T\) structures that don’t become each other by restricting to e.g. \(T\ge 0\).

Now check candidates.

---

### 1.
\(T^{c0}c1\epsilon^{c2}+c3\epsilon+c4\epsilon^{c5}+c6\epsilon^2+c7\epsilon^{c8}+c9\epsilon^{c2}\)

No exponential in \(1/T\). Also no way to create both \(\epsilon T\) and \(\epsilon^{b}T\) simultaneously: only one \(T\)-dependent term \(T^{c0}\epsilon^{c2}\). GT needs two different \(T\)-dependent powers of \(\epsilon\) (one with \(\epsilon^1\), one with \(\epsilon^{1.450...}\)). Not possible. **No match.**

### 2.

### 23.
\(T c0\epsilon + T c1\epsilon^{c2} + c3\epsilon + c4\epsilon^{c2} + c5\epsilon^{c6} + c7\epsilon^{c8}\exp(c9/T)\)

This is closer: it has
- \(T\epsilon\) term (good for GT’s \(\epsilon T\)),
- \(T\epsilon^{c2}\) term (could match GT’s \(\epsilon^{1.450...}T\) by setting \(c2=1.45029456614\)),
- and \(\epsilon^{c8}\exp(c9/T)\) (set \(c8=0.31784974436\), \(c9=-49.4558232675/8.314\)).

But GT’s first term is \(\epsilon(\alpha T+\beta)\) with a specific intercept \(\beta\epsilon\) and slope \(\alpha \epsilon T\). Candidate can do that using \(T c0\epsilon + c3\epsilon\). Good.

GT’s third term is \(2.30405\,\epsilon^{1.450...}(T-278.1478751)=2.30405\,T\epsilon^{1.450...}- (2.30405\cdot278.1478751)\epsilon^{1.450...}\).
Candidate has \(T c1\epsilon^{c2}\) to match the \(2.30405\,T\epsilon^{1.450...}\) part, and it also has a **non-\(T\)** \(\epsilon^{c2}\) term \(c4\epsilon^{c2}\) to match the \(- (2.30405\cdot278.1478751)\epsilon^{1.450...}\) part. Perfect.

So we can set:
- \(c2 = 1.450294566141342\)
- \(c1 = 2.304053848821008\)
- \(c4 = -2.304053848821008 \cdot 278.14787512499896\)
- Exponential term: \(c8 = 0.3178497443603504\), \(c7 = 98.57939495694947\), \(c9 = -49.45582326747874/8.314\)
- First affine-\(T\) epsilon term: need
  \[
  61.3468690640\,\epsilon\left(-0.0507652233(T-278.1478751)+1\right)
  = (61.3468690640\cdot -0.0507652233)\,T\epsilon + 61.3468690640(0.0507652233\cdot278.1478751+1)\epsilon
  \]
  So set \(c0 = 61.3468690640\cdot(-0.0507652233)\) and \(c3\) to the intercept coefficient above.

Also set \(c5=0\) to remove \(c5\epsilon^{c6}\) (or set \(c5=0\) directly).

Thus candidate 23 can match GT **globally** (no special domain restriction needed, aside from usual \(T\neq 0\) for the exponential term, which is consistent with GT anyway). **Match.**
